SUMMARY OF FINDINGS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
The Rockfall Hazard Rating System RHRS program established for the City and
County of Honolulu in 2002 was updated in 2008 2009 Database Update No 1 to reflect
current information pertaining to the slope inventory ranking of the slopes and conceptual
rockfall hazard mitigation designs This Volume 6 report presents current information
compiled during Database Update No 1 pertaining to the conceptual remedial designs
and construction cost estimates for the Class A slope sites
The City and County of Honolulu RHRS program is based on the National Highway
Institute NHI and Federal Highway Administration FHWA RHRS and is maintained to
provide a slope inventory and classification of potential rockfall hazard sites adjacent to
City streets on the Island of Oahu Hawaii The RHRS program consists of six stages
1 Rock Slope Inventory 2 Preliminary Slope Rating 3 Detailed Slope Rating
4 Conceptual Design and Cost Estimate 5 Project Identification and Development and
6 Review and Database Update
Based on the findings of the RHRS Database Update No 1 for Stages 1 through 3
conducted in 2008 there are 59 rockfall slope sections that have been assessed an A
classification 93 slope sections with a B classification and 105 slope sections with a C
classification
This Volume 6 report presents the Stage 4 Conceptual Designs and Construction
Cost Estimates for the 59 Class A slopes contained in the current City and County
of Honolulu rock slope inventory in general accordance with the established procedures
for the RHRS program outlined in the FHWA Publication No dated
November 1993
The text and appendices of this report should be referred to for discussion and
presentation of the findings derived from Database Update No 1 of the conceptual
remedial designs and construction cost estimates
END OF SUMMARY OF FINDINGS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
Page 1
Hawaii California
SECTION 1 GENERAL
1 1
Introduction
This report presents the results of our geotechnical engineering evaluation in
support of Database Update No 1 for Stage 4 Conceptual Designs and Cost
Estimates of the multi stage RHRS program This work product carries forward with
Database Update No 1 conducted for RHRS Stages 1 through 3 which are
summarized in report Volumes 1 through 5
This Volume 6 report summarizes our work efforts and presents our findings
associated with the performance of the RHRS Stage 4 Conceptual Designs and Cost
Estimates for the Class A slopes identified in the current Rock Slope Inventory for City
streets on the Island of Oahu Our work was performed in general accordance with the
Federal Highways Administration RHRS program which was initially developed and
implemented by the Oregon Department of Transportation ODOT and the National
Highway Institute NHI The City and County of Honolulu RHRS program continues to
evolve since its inception which occurred over 7 years ago The updated findings
presented in this report are based on our research field evaluation and engineering
analyses conducted for the City and County of Honolulu Rock Slide Potential
Inspections project The Stage 4 Conceptual Designs and Cost Estimates is an integral
component that supports the prioritization of remedial construction to reduce the
potential hazards associated with potential rockfall activity The findings presented
herein are subject to the limitations noted at the end of this report
1 2
Project Considerations
Many of the public streets owned and maintained by the City and County of
Honolulu traverse steep hillside terrain throughout the Island of Oahu Due to the steep
terrain many of the City streets are below developed cut slopes and natural hillsides
composed of basaltic rock altered by varying degrees of weathering and erosion
Erosion of the slopes by exposure to weathering construction activity and ground
SECTION 1 GENERAL
W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
Page 2
Hawaii California
vibration from heavy traffic may result in rockfall that has the potential to produce
hazards to public safety
It is desired to proactively construct remedial stabilization and or protective
systems to reduce the potential hazards associated with rockfall activity However
because of the large number of potential rockfall sites and limited construction funds it
is necessary to systematically classify the potential rockfall hazard along these roads in
order to establish a rational way to categorize and prioritize remedial construction work
Thus the Rockfall Hazard Rating System program is being utilized to facilitate the
categorization and prioritization of the work The information obtained from the field
studies including the conceptual remedial designs and cost estimates is best managed
by a computer database Rockfall Database Management Program RDMP developed
specifically for the project
The RHRS is a comprehensive process that allows responsible agencies to
actively manage the rock slopes adjacent to their roadway system In general the
RHRS process consists of 6 stages that build upon each other to achieve the ultimate
objective of assisting the prioritization and planning of remedial construction work The
6 stages of the program are outlined as follows
1
Rock Slope Inventory Specific information on rockfall sites are gathered
Information required includes an inventory of all City owned streets from
City GIS maps and street index book delineation of streets with rock
slopes from geologic and soil maps and records of past rockfall activity
from the City
2
Preliminary Slope Rating Potential rockfall sections are grouped into
three broad classes A B and C This step eliminates the sites with
minimal or no rockfall potential Class C and separate sites with higher
potential Class A from those with less potential Class B in order to
focus the effort on the sites with higher risk
SECTION 1 GENERAL
W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
Page 3
Hawaii California
3
Detailed Slope Rating A numerical rating is assessed to selected sites
Class A slopes in order to categorize risk and prioritize remedial work
The rating system incorporates factors such as slope height ditch
effectiveness traffic volume sight distance roadway width geologic
characteristics climate and rockfall history A numerical score is
assigned based on these factors in order to quantify the rating The
numerical scores assist in the prioritization of the remedial projects
4
Conceptual Design and Cost Estimate Appropriate concept level
remedial designs are proposed along with preliminary construction cost
estimates in order to assist in the prioritization of the remedial repair
projects
5
Project Identification and Development The information gathered in the
previous steps are used to develop a priority list for remediation projects
Several different approaches may be used based on cost rockfall risk
property ownership cost benefit location and other factors
6
Review and Database Update All of the slopes contained within the
slope inventory are reviewed periodically to evaluate whether changes
have occurred which affect the scoring Database updates should be
performed if necessary at intervals of about 5 years
As mentioned previously the RHRS program was initially developed in 2002 and
included Stages 1 through 4 Subsequently Stage 5 was recently implemented by
selecting four high hazard potential rockfall sites for remediation project development
The current task is for Stage 6 to review and update the database developed in 2002
Database Update No 1 for Stages 1 through 3 of the Rockfall Hazard Rating
System which include the rock slope inventory preliminary slope classifications
Classes A B or C and detailed slope rating of the Class A slopes are
presented in the Volume 1 through Volume 5 reports This report identified as
Volume 6 presents the preliminary conceptual remedial designs and construction cost
estimates for the 59 Class A slopes contained in the project slope inventory
1 3

The purpose of the RHRS Stage 4 study is to develop preliminary concept level
designs and construction cost estimates for the 59 Class A rated slope sites contained

SECTION 2 DISCUSSION
2 1
Objective
The objective for the RHRS Stage 4 Database Update No 1 as applied to the
City and County of Honolulu Rock Slide Potential Inspections study is to review and
update the concept level remedial design alternatives and construction cost estimates
to reflect current information and costs for the 55 Class A slopes contained in the
project slope inventory
It should be noted that four high hazard potential rockfall sites are currently under
mitigation design Stage 5 Therefore the conceptual designs and cost estimates
provided herein only pertain to the remaining 55 Class A slopes
The conceptual designs and cost estimates are intended to provide an additional
basis for the planning and prioritization of remedial construction projects The
completion of Stage 4 concludes the information collection process for the Class A
slopes and the beginning of the project development stage RHRS Stage 5
2 2
Methods
The development of the conceptual designs and construction cost estimates for
this project is based on the general approach documented in the FHWA Rockfall
Hazard Rating System RHRS technical manual Publication No 057
dated November 1993
Thirty 30 conceptual remedial alternative schemes for rockfall hazard mitigation
were developed for this project The conceptual remedial alternatives were developed
through our initial research study conducted for the establishment of the RHRS program
as applied to the City and County of Honolulu Rock Slide Potential Inspections project in
2002 For this update the various remedial alternatives have been reviewed and
updated to reflect current information and or new technical developments related to the
remedial schemes
SECTION 2 DISCUSSION
W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
Page 6
Hawaii California
Based on the compiled field and research information the 55 Class A slope
sites were reviewed in detail to evaluate and select appropriate conceptual remedial
alternatives which could be implemented to reduce the potential rockfall hazard In
general selection of the site specific conceptual remedial alternatives was based on our
consideration of the existing slope and site geometry anticipated slope ownership
geology constructability and general construction costs For each Class A slope site
two or three potentially viable conceptual remedial alternatives were selected The
proposed remedial alternatives are provided for the owner design engineer s
consideration and are not listed in order of importance or preference
The Site and Conceptual Alternative Summary sheets presented in Appendix A
provide a brief summary description of each slope site and the proposed remedial
alternatives with some associated advantages and disadvantages Each of the 55 Class
A slope sites are presented in Appendix A on Plates A 1 through A 59
Thirty idealized drawings depicting the general components of the remedial
alternatives were developed to assist in the illustration of the proposed improvements
The drawings schematically illustrate the main components comprising the proposed
remedial alternatives The thirty Remedial Alternative Concept Drawings are presented
in Appendix B on Plates B 1 through B 30
Based on our proposed conceptual design schemes the basic construction and
material components were itemized to assist in the development of the preliminary
construction cost estimates The unit costs were compiled from our experience and
research of local costs for materials and labor The Cost Estimate Breakdown sheets
presented in Appendix C on Plates C 1 through C 59 provide a breakdown of the
estimated construction costs for each of the 59 Class A slopes A table summarizing
the 59 Cost Estimate Breakdown sheets contained in Appendix C is presented on
Plates 1 1 and 1 2
It should be emphasized that most of the conceptual remedial alternatives
presented in this Database Update No 1 focus on long term engineered solutions
SECTION 2 DISCUSSION
W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
Page 7
Hawaii California
designed to reduce the potential hazard associated with potential rockfall activity Other
short term remedial options which may consist of the removal of loose rocks and talus
accumulations from the slope or the installation of standard chain link type fencing are
considered to be interim remedial measures that may temporarily lower the risk
associated with potential rockfall activity Short term remedial work may require
repeated performance or replacement of the improvements to maintain the reduction in
risk In addition short term remedial work may not provide protection against larger
rockfalls triggered by erosion and heavy runoff However the implementation of these
interim non engineered remedial alternatives may be considered if long term or
permanent remedial action cannot be undertaken
We have included the installation of traditional chain link fencing at the slope toe
as a possible short term remedial measure The alternative is identified as Conceptual
Remedial Alternative No 30 and is considered a non engineered temporary measure
that may be used where no other viable alternative can be constructed within the City
Right Of Way The purpose for the installation of chain link fencing is to reduce the
accumulation of debris in the public Right Of Way The use of chain link fencing as a
long term remedial alternative is not recommended to protect against hazardous rockfall
conditions because the materials and construction of traditional chain link fencing has
minimal ability to contain larger rock impact force It is our opinion that chain link fencing
should be used only as an interim remedial measure until other long term slope
stabilization or rock containment structures are constructed to reduce the potential for
rockfall encroachment on the public Right Of Way
2 3
Conceptual Remedial Alternatives
The 30 conceptual remedial alternatives developed for this project are remedial
scheme variations derived from 10 primary rockfall mitigation controls commonly
employed in the rockfall mitigation industry Elements comprising the 10 primary
controls were selected and combined to develop the 30 conceptual remedial
alternatives for this project The 10 primary rockfall mitigation controls used to develop
the various 30 conceptual remedial alternatives for this project are as follows

New Cut Slope Development
The 30 conceptual remedial alternatives were developed to address the
mitigation of potential rockfall hazards on the slopes adjacent to City and County of
Honolulu roadways The 30 conceptual remedial alternatives were developed to
address both the current slope sites and the possible future slopes sites that may be
added to the database Slight variations of the 30 remedial alternatives may be
proposed on an individual site basis to account for varying site conditions and possible
constraints Typical schematic drawings were developed to illustrate the remedial
alternatives including the general components and geometry of the conceptual level
design The schematic drawings referenced in the Site and Conceptual Alternative
Summaries are presented in Appendix B The following table presents a summary of
the 30 remedial conceptual alternatives with the remedial alternative reference titles and

2 4
Site and Conceptual Alternative Summary
The Site and Conceptual Alternative Summary sheets present a summarized
description of the general site conditions and the proposed remedial alternatives for
each of the 59 Class A sites The descriptive format presents an overview of the
general site conditions In addition the proposed conceptual remedial alternatives are
described to provide a general overview of the probable site specific issues that may be
considered in the design stage Some general advantages and disadvantages related
to the remedial alternatives are also presented for consideration
The Site and Conceptual Alternative Summary sheets are presented in
Appendix A Plates A 1 through A 59 and are arranged in order from the highest score
slope to the lowest score slope
2 5
Preliminary Construction Cost Estimate
A preliminary construction cost estimate for each of the proposed remedial
alternatives is presented on the Cost Estimate Breakdown sheet The cost estimate
provided reflects the preliminary estimate of the construction cost only based on year
2008 2009 prices Other costs such as Right Of Way acquisition contingency
overhead and profit taxes and bonding and engineering design are excluded from the
preliminary cost estimate The purpose for the preliminary construction cost estimate is
to provide cost information that may be used for comparison to assist in the prioritization
and appropriation of budgets for the remedial projects
The Cost Estimate Breakdown sheets are presented in Appendix C Plates C 1
through C 59 and are arranged in order from the highest scored slope to the lowest
scored slope
Plates 1 1 and 1 2 present a summary of the 59 Class A slopes which are
ranked according to their RHRS numerical scores and the remedial conceptual
alternatives and preliminary construction cost estimates for each of the slope sites
SECTION 2 DISCUSSION

2 6
Considerations for Project Development
Stage 5 of the RHRS program consists of remedial project identification and
development Projects may be advanced to the development stage by prioritizing the
remedial work using the information collected in the preceding stages of the RHRS
program
The Stage 5 Project Identification and Development stage is essentially the final
phase of the prioritization of remedial work The computer Rockfall Database
Management Program RDMP is an integral tool used by trained personnel to sort and
query the information to assist in the identification and development of projects for
construction Projects may be advanced by various methods which may include one or
more of the following criteria using the information collected during the previous stages
of the RHRS program
Projects may be advanced on the basis of their detailed rating
numerical score
Projects may be advanced based on their numerical scores relative
to their estimated construction cost
Projects may be advanced on the basis of having similar remedial
designs
Projects may be advanced based on the site location
Projects may be advanced based on the slope ownership condition
It should be emphasized that many of the slope sites are affected by varying
slope ownership conditions Based on a preliminary review of available property
ownership information it is anticipated that some slopes may be entirely within private
property or may be only partially within the City Right Of Way In other cases the
slopes may be mostly within State of Hawaii or Federal property Furthermore for a
given slope segment the limit of the City Right Of Way may range from near the top of
the slope to the toe of the slope depending on location along the slope segment
Therefore we believe that the development of prospective remedial projects should
begin with the field identification staking of the existing property boundary to
definitively identify the slope ownership condition This step is necessary to assist in the
SECTION 2 DISCUSSION
W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
Page 12
Hawaii California
selection of a viable remedial alternative since some alternatives may require the
procurement of construction easements or additional Right Of Way acquisition
In addition to the identification and staking of existing property boundaries a
current topographic survey of the slope will be necessary to support additional detailed
study design work and the preparation of construction plans for the rockfall mitigation
projects Archaeological assessments of some slopes may be necessary to identify
archaeological features and possible restrictions that may affect remedial construction
Finally it is recommended that the site numerical ratings and related information
be reviewed at about 5 year intervals to allow the opportunity to update or revise the
information pertaining to the existing site conditions and possible remedial alternatives

SECTION 3 LIMITATIONS
The findings interpretations and recommendations submitted in this data report
are based in part upon information obtained from research the use of available public
information and site observations Variation in slope conditions between and beyond
our preliminary observations may occur and the nature and extent of these variations
may not become evident until additional detailed site evaluation or construction is
underway If variations then appear evident Geolabs should be contacted to
re evaluate the preliminary recommendations presented in this report
The location and limits of the slope sites rockfall sections are approximate
having been estimated by taping from property corner reference points and visible
features shown on the available Tax Key Maps obtained from the City s GIS information
database The physical location of the slope sites should be considered accurate only
to the degree implied by the methods used
The site observations which contribute to the basis of the development of the
conceptual remedial alternatives and construction cost estimates depict the general
surface conditions observed at the time of our site visit thus some difference in site
observations should be anticipated from site visits made at different times Experienced
personnel implemented the field evaluations and professional judgments were
exercised to evaluate the existing site conditions with respect to the presence of
adverse structural geology and possible remedial work that may be appropriate on a
site specific basis The field data has been reviewed and interpretations made in the
formulation of this report
The preliminary cost estimates provided in this report are based on anticipated
Year 2008 2009 local costs for labor and materials for assumed quantities based on the
estimation performed exclusive of construction plans As such the preliminary cost
estimates contained herein are intended solely for comparison use to support the
selection of viable remedial alternatives and the prioritization of the remedial projects
SECTION 3 LIMITATIONS

This report has been prepared for the exclusive use of the City and County of
Honolulu Department of Design and Construction and other project consultants for
specific application to the Rockfall Hazard Rating System RHRS as applied to the City
and County of Honolulu Rock Slide Potential Inspections Project in accordance with
generally accepted geotechnical engineering principles and practices No warranty is
expressed or implied
This report has been prepared solely for the purpose of presenting the results of
the conceptual design alternatives and preliminary cost estimates RHRS Stage 4 in
general accordance with the FHWA Rockfall Hazard Rating System program The
information is intended for the preliminary evaluation of potential rockfall hazards for
City streets on the Island of Oahu Therefore this report may not contain sufficient
data or the proper information to serve as the basis for preparation of construction cost
estimates nor for bidding purposes A contractor wishing to bid on this project should
retain a competent geotechnical engineer to assist in the interpretation of this report
and or in the performance of additional site specific exploration for bid estimation
purposes
The owner client should be aware that unanticipated soil rock conditions are
commonly encountered Unforeseen conditions such as hillslope evolution inactive
landslides variable groundwater conditions soft deposits hard layers or cavities may
occur in localized areas and may require additional evaluation or corrections in the field
Therefore a sufficient contingency fund is recommended to accommodate these
possible extra costs
This geotechnical engineering evaluation was not intended to investigate the
potential presence of hazardous materials existing at the site The equipment
techniques and personnel used to conduct a geo environmental exploration differ
substantially from those applied in a geotechnical engineering study
END OF LIMITATIONS

SITE AND CONCEPTUAL ALTERNATIVE SUMMARY
Phase III Rock Slide Potential Inspections
Rockfall Hazard Rating System Database Update No 1
Project No 01154
Various Locations Oahu Hawaii
W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
PLATE A 1 1
A Slope ID No
1
Preliminary Slope I D No
099
City Street Road Name
Pupukea Road
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The lengthy rock slope is located along a narrow roadway corridor that provides the only
access to the upland Pupukea residential area The slope mainly consists of rock cut
slopes consisting of interbedded massive fractured basalt rock and clinker In general
the cut slope is irregular in character with many large overhanging blocks bounded by
weak severely fractured clinker layers Evidence of past rockfall and landslide activity
was locally observed The cut slope appears to transition into moderately to densely
vegetated natural mixed rock and soil slopes that extend up toward a series of adjacent
residential properties Other large fractured rock outcrops are visible locally on the
upper natural slopes The cut slopes vary in height with the taller cut slopes located at
the middle to southern half of the slope segment The northern part of the slope segment
near the tight radius horseshoe roadway curve contains some lower cut slopes on the
order of about 10 to 20 feet in height followed by extensive upper natural rock slopes
extending up the mountainside There is no sidewalk or curb and gutter improvement
and a sharp topographic drop off bounded by a guardrail exists on the makai side of the
roadway Underground utilities were not observed within the roadway except some
possible drainage structures Overhead utilities appear to be limited to street light poles
The cut slope appears to be located at least partly to mostly within the existing roadway
right of way City property The upper natural slopes appear to be located within the
adjacent 9 private properties The potential hazard consists of potentially large blocks of
falling rock materials that may encroach directly upon the roadway In addition some
shallow landslides involving mixed soil and weathered rock may affect the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
To be determined by the mitigation design
SITE AND CONCEPTUAL ALTERNATIVE SUMMARY
Phase III Rock Slide Potential Inspections
Rockfall Hazard Rating System Database Update No 1
Project No 01154
Various Locations Oahu Hawaii
W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
PLATE A 2 1
A Slope ID No
2
Preliminary Slope I D No
050
City Street Road Name
Sierra Drive
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock slope is located along a main roadway in a residential community Based on
the character of the rock slope materials the slope segment is divided into two regions
consisting of a northeastern cut slope region and a southwestern cut slope region The
northeastern cut slope is composed mostly of large block open fractured basalt rock
whereas the southwestern cut slope is composed mostly of welded spatter lava basaltic
clinker The very steep slopes are moderately vegetated with shrubs and some large
trees Existing homes with associated retaining walls and fences are located very close
to the crest of the slope There are curb improvements at the site in addition to a
sidewalk and retaining wall along the opposite side of the narrow roadway Overhead
utility lines and light poles are located on both sides of portions of the road with utility
lateral lines traversing up the slope from the road There is also an existing private
stairway and private vehicle parking space cut into the base of the slope at the site The
cut slope appears to be located mostly within the adjacent six residential properties The
potential hazard consists of potentially large blocks of falling rock and smaller rock
fragments that may encroach upon the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
To be determined by the mitigation design
SITE AND CONCEPTUAL ALTERNATIVE SUMMARY
Phase III Rock Slide Potential Inspections
Rockfall Hazard Rating System Database Update No 1
Project No 01154
Various Locations Oahu Hawaii

GEOLABS INC
PLATE A 3 1
A Slope ID No
3
Preliminary Slope I D No
066 B
City Street Road Name
Prospect Street
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock slope segment is located along a main roadway in a residential community on
the western slope of Punchbowl Crater The slope segment consists of highly fractured
rock cut slopes and upper natural hillslopes composed of generally low relief rock
material covered by thin soils The cut slopes are composed of adversely bedded
open fractured volcanic tuff which may produce individual large blocks of broken rock or
localized regions of rockslide activity Evidence of past rockfall and rockslide activity on
the cut slopes was observed In general the natural slopes that extend upward toward
the crater rim appear to have few rock outcrop exposures with the exception of a portion
of the slope located about midway along the slope segment There is no sidewalk or
curb and gutter improvement at the site Some underground utilities including hydrants
and utility poles are located along portions of the base of the slope A widened and
unpaved shoulder area used for parking is located along the base of the slope at the
northern two thirds of the slope segment The southern third of the slope segment has
existing cut slopes located closely adjacent to the roadway with minimal existing
shoulder area The cut slopes appear to be located mostly within the adjacent Federal
property The potential hazard consists of potential rock cut slope instability that may
produce possible large blocks of falling rock material that may encroach upon the
shoulder parking and roadway areas
Conceptual Design Alternatives
To be determined by the mitigation design

GEOLABS INC
PLATE A 4 1
A Slope ID No
4
Preliminary Slope I D No
062 N
City Street Road Name
Round Top Drive
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The volcanic tuff cut slope is along an arterial route serving a rural residential community
and scenic drive The slope consists of a steep cut slope adjacent to the road Other
flatter but heavily vegetated natural slopes extend upward toward the top of the
ridgeline Rockfall appears to be produced by the exposed cut slope as the hillside
above generally consists of moderately sloping lower relief terrain assumed to be
mantled by cinder soils with limited rock outcrops There are no sidewalk or curb and
gutter improvements at the site and the existing unpaved road shoulder is about 3 to 4
feet wide Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way
is at or near the top of the cut slope Existing underground and overhead utilities were
not observed The potential hazard consists of potential rockfall involving large block
size material that may topple or slide and encroach upon the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Soldier Pile In Fill Concrete Retaining Wall
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose rock materials from the slope face
Careful scaling should be performed on the upper slope above the proposed retaining
wall height The alternative consists of the construction of a concrete retaining wall of
about 15 feet in height in the shoulder area along the base of the slope In general the
concrete retaining wall consists of a row of soldier piles supported by drilled shaft
foundations with concrete wall panels that are installed between the soldier piles The
purpose of the concrete retaining wall is to provide rockfall protection and permanent
stabilization of the lower slope face
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including road closure
The existing utilities are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 18
Advantages
Improvements could be constructed within the existing Right Of Way
The concrete retaining wall should provide permanent low maintenance cut
slope stabilization and rockfall protection
SITE AND CONCEPTUAL ALTERNATIVE SUMMARY

W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
PLATE A 4 2
Disadvantages
Higher construction cost
Concrete wall appearance
Permanent removal of vegetation from the lower slope
Upper portion of the cut slope above the retaining wall would remain exposed
No 2 Slope Setback
This alternative consists of excavating the existing steep rock cut slope to produce a
minimum 15 foot wide setback from the existing toe of the slope The purpose for the
new slope setback is to develop a sloping catchment area of about 15 feet wide adjacent
to the roadway Warning signs would be installed along the catchment area The new
rock cut slope may be designed at an inclination of 1H 4V since a catchment area is to
be developed below the new cut slope The new cut slope excavation should improve
the existing cut slope deficiencies by removing the existing unstable blocks of rock and
other erosional irregularities that have developed over the years
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including lane closure and
contra flow of traffic Existing utilities in the area are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 25
Advantages
Considered a low maintenance rockfall protection measure provision of a
catchment area
Should improve cut slope stability by removing existing potentially unstable slope
materials and previous failure features
Maintain natural rock cut slope appearance in the scenic area
Disadvantages
Need for additional right of way acquisition to encompass new cut slope
Significant volume of rock excavation required
Higher cut slope will be developed

PLATE A 4 3
No 3 Anchored Wire Cable Mesh
This alternative consists of vegetation cutting the scaling of loose rock materials from
the slope and the construction of anchored wire mesh on the slope face The wire mesh
is anchored pinned to the slope face to aid in the stabilization and retention of the slope
materials since only a limited road shoulder is available The purpose of the
improvement is to stabilize the slope face and protect the roadway from potential falling
rock hazards
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with a lane closure
Existing utilities are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 7
Advantages
Minimal slope excavation
Anchored wire mesh should increase the slope face stability
Designated slope toe catchment area is not necessary
Disadvantages
Some extension of the City Right Of Way may be necessary to accommodate
top of slope ground anchor installation
Temporary vegetation removal
Need for periodic inspection and possible future maintenance of the mesh
Existing narrow road shoulder would remain
Wire mesh appearance on the slope face

PLATE A 5 1
A Slope ID No
5
Preliminary Slope I D No
089 D
City Street Road Name
Waihona Street
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock slope is located along an arterial roadway that serves the Pearl City industrial
and commercial district The tall slope estimated to be about 80 to 90 feet high is
composed of large block type fractured basalt rock and segments of the slope stand
nearly vertical An existing sidewalk traverses the base of the slope and an additional flat
area existing slope setback of about 10 feet or less exists between the sidewalk and
the base of the slope The existing setback area contains some very large blocks of
rock about 6 to 10 feet diameter that appear to have fallen from the slope
Underground utilities may be located beneath the sidewalk adjacent to the slope and
utility poles with electric lines are located along the base of the slope Street parking is
currently permitted along the slope side of the roadway The tall slope appears to be
located mostly within two adjacent private owned properties The potential hazard
consists of falling rock materials consisting of very large blocks of rock and boulders that
may encroach upon the street parking area and roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
To be determined by the mitigation design

PLATE A 6 1
A Slope ID No
6
Preliminary Slope I D No
111 A
City Street Road Name
Maunawili Road
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The mixed rock and soil cut slope is composed of semi consolidated older alluvium
consisting of various weathered cobbles and some boulders embedded in a soil matrix
The older alluvial deposits are overlain by highly to extremely weathered basalt rock
The slope is located along a secondary access roadway that serves a residential
community Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of
Way is at or near the top of the slope The existing slope has experienced significant
erosion including small landslides and the raveling of embedded rocks from the slope
The upper slope is densely overgrown with dense Hao tree growth Underground utilities
such as water and sewer are located within the roadway A very steep slope leading
down toward a stream is located on the opposite side of the road from the cut slope
Some utility service laterals are located on the slope face Improvements such as curb
and gutters or sidewalks are not present The toe of the slope composed of loose
eroded soils and some rock fragments appears to encroach on the travel lane surface
The potential hazard consists of eroded soils and some falling rock materials that
encroach upon the roadway due to the lack of a shoulder
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Roadway Widening with Cantilever Deck
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose rock materials trimming of the existing
top of slope earth root overhangs and the widening of the existing roadway to provide
for the development of a minimum 10 foot wide catchment area bounded by a concrete
Jersey barrier The roadway widening may be accomplished by constructing a
cantilevered deck extension of a minimum of about 6 feet wide along the existing outer
edge of the road Drilled shaft foundations constructed within the existing roadway
surface would support the cantilevered deck The purpose of the improvements is to
develop a catchment area at the base of the cut slope within the existing narrow
roadway corridor bounded by steep slopes
The construction activity is anticipated to require closure of the roadway and diversion of
traffic to an alternate route It is anticipated that the existing underground utilities may
need to be relocated or protected The existing service laterals on the slope may not be
affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 28
SITE AND CONCEPTUAL ALTERNATIVE SUMMARY
Phase III Rock Slide Potential Inspections

Considered a rockfall and landslide protection measure
Creation of a catchment ditch separate from the roadway

Disadvantages
Extension of the City Right Of Way to encompass roadway improvements
Slope stability not substantially improved
Underground utility relocation required
Periodic cleanup of debris from within the catchment area required

Higher construction cost
No 2 Soldier Pile In Fill Concrete Retaining Wall
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose rock materials from the slope and the
construction of a reinforced concrete retaining wall of about 16 feet in height along the
lower portion of the slope In general the concrete retaining wall consists of a row of
soldier piles supported by drilled shaft foundations with concrete wall panels that are
installed between the soldier piles A drainage interceptor ditch would be constructed
along the top of the retaining wall The concrete retaining wall would cover most of the
lower and middle slope face In addition the remaining exposed upper portion of the
existing cut slope would be faced with Grouted Rubble Pavement GRP to protect
against erosion The purpose of the improvements is to stabilize the slope against future
erosion including potential rockfall and soil erosion
The construction activity is anticipated to require closure of the roadway and diversion of
traffic to an alternate route It is anticipated that the existing underground utilities may
need to be relocated or protected The existing service laterals on the slope will also
need to be relocated or protected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 18

070 D
City Street Road Name
Pacific Heights Road
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock slope is along a narrow arterial roadway serving a residential community
Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way is at and
near the top of the cut slope There is an existing concrete drainage swale along the
base of the slope Sidewalks and other curb and gutter improvements are not present at
the site The slope segment mainly consists of a steep fractured thin bedded rock cut
slope with some existing privately owned walls along the crest of the slope Some
existing utility lateral lines traverse the slope face In addition some trees including a
large banyan with substantial surface roots were observed growing on the slope face
The potential hazard consists of falling rock materials that may encroach upon the
roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Shotcrete Slope Facing
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose rock materials from the slope face and
the application of reinforced shotcrete material as a slope facing If the banyan tree and
root system cannot be completely removed the shotcrete must be applied around the
existing root system The purpose of the shotcrete application is to reduce the surface
erosion of the exposed slope face by constructing a thin continuous layer of reinforced
concrete grout on the slope face
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with a periodic lane
closure Utility laterals traversing the slope face may require relocation
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 11
Advantages
Could be substantially constructed within the existing Right Of Way limit
Eliminates erosion of the exposed slope surface and subsequent debris clean up
Lower maintenance needs expected
Lower construction cost

Need for intensive slope scaling and permanent removal of vegetation roots and
trees for site preparation
Existing banyan tree roots must be removed from the slope face or shotcrete
must be placed around the root system
May require some additional stabilization of potentially unstable rock blocks or
filling of voids prior to shotcrete application
Concrete surface appearance

performance
No 2 Anchored Wire Cable Mesh
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose rock materials from the slope and the
construction of anchored wire mesh on the slope face The wire mesh is anchored
pinned to the slope face to aid in the stabilization and retention of the slope materials
The purpose of the improvement is to stabilize the slope face and protect the roadway
from potential falling rock hazards
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with a lane closure
Existing utility laterals traversing up the slope will require relocation or reconstruction
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 7

Limited need for debris cleanup
Disadvantages

No 3 Draped Wire Mesh
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose rock materials from the slope face and
the installation of draped wire mesh panels on the slope face The purpose of the draped
wire mesh is to control the fall of rock materials toward the existing concrete swale
located along the base of the slope
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with periodic lane
closures Utility laterals traversing the slope face may require protection during
construction or relocation
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 1

ground anchor installation
Draped system only with limited ground anchors for slope stabilization

PLATE A 8 1
A Slope ID No
8
Preliminary Slope I D No
062 Q
City Street Road Name
Round Top Drive
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The slope segment is along a rural arterial scenic drive and consists of a near
continuous length of cut banks and slopes along a narrow roadway with very limited
existing shoulder space The slopes appear to consist of variable materials including
mainly saprolitic soils cemented cinder and some fractured basalt rock The slope
segment appears to have experienced localized landslide activity and many parts of the
slope segment appear to be affected by surface erosion In some places large leaning
trees located on or above the slope may contribute to the cut slope instability The slope
is very densely vegetated with shrubs and trees with flatter natural slopes above the cut
slope portion Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of
Way is at or near the top of the cut slopes adjacent to private property The City Right
Of Way is currently undetermined where the road passes adjacent to State of Hawaii
property Existing overhead utilities and poles were observed at the site Existing
underground utilities appear to consist of storm drain inlets and pipes Improvements
such as curb and gutters and sidewalks are not present The potential hazard consists of
slope surface erosion areas of landslide activity and large unstable trees growing on
the slope that may encroach upon the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Concrete Retaining Wall
This alternative consists of vegetation cutting slope debris removal scaling of loose
rock materials from the slope face and the construction of a reinforced concrete
retaining wall of about 10 feet in height along the base of the slopes The purpose of the
improvements is to stabilize the cut slope landslide activity and erosion and rockfall
conditions along the lower slope face
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control consisting of lane and
road closures Existing drainage utilities and utility poles at the base of the slopes will
need to be relocated or reconstructed
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 17
Advantages
May be substantially constructed within the existing Right Of Way
Considered a permanent slope stabilization and erosion control measure
Minimal future maintenance and cleaning of debris from roadway
May help to reduce the overhanging vegetation condition on the slopes

No 2 Anchored Wire Cable Mesh
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose soil rock and woody vegetation
materials from the slope and the construction of anchored wire mesh on the slope face
Due to the variable material composition of the slope and the lack of space for roadside
catchment of debris the wire mesh is anchored pinned to the slope face to aid in the
stabilization and retention of the deeper slope materials It is recommended that
corrosion resistant mesh materials be utilized in this wet environment Some stable
lower height cut slopes and banks composed cemented cinder material may be
covered with anchored erosion control matting in place of anchored wire mesh The
erosion control matting may consist of Percussion Driven Earth Anchor Mat PDEA
matting The purpose of the improvements is to stabilize the existing cut slope face and
protect the roadway form potential shallow soil erosion landslide activity and some
areas of potential rockfall hazard
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control consisting of lane and
road closures Existing utilities must be protected during construction
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 7
Advantages
Anchored wire mesh should increase the slope stability against shallow slides
and surface erosion
PDEA matting may be used in more stable and low height slope settings to
reduce surface erosion
Improvements should cover the full slope height
Less visually obtrusive
Ground cover vegetation should re establish itself quickly due to the wet
environment
The removal of overhanging trees should aid in the slope stability

PLATE A 9 1
A Slope ID No
9
Preliminary Slope I D No
085
City Street Road Name
Moanalua Loop
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock cut slope is along a main thoroughfare in a residential and commercial district
The cut slope is composed of large block type fractured basalt rock that may produce
rockfall consisting of very large boulders and blocks of rock The basalt rock cut slope
encompasses massive rock formation containing many open fractures The massive
type rock formation is undercut by weakened clinker at the southern end of the slope
segment There is no sidewalk fronting the slope however an unpaved shoulder exists
with space currently used for vehicle parking Curb and gutter roadway improvements
are not present Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of
Way is at or near the top of the cut slope Overhead utility lines and poles are present on
the opposite side of the roadway and underground utilities do not appear to be present
Two utility guy poles and concrete drain inlets reside along the toe of the slope The
potential hazard consists of falling rock material consisting of very large blocks of rock
and boulders that may encroach upon the roadway
It is imperative that the potential rockfall hazards on the upper flatter slope surfaces be
carefully evaluated for removal or stabilization in place since the proposed remedial
alternatives do not address the potential rockfall originating from these upper private
owned slope surfaces The existing upper slope gradients do not appear to be conducive
to rockfall initiation however the large sized of the existing blocks of rock warrants
special attention
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Roadway Reconfiguration to Develop Catchment Area
This alternative consists of the intensive scaling of loose rock materials from the cut
slope face especially the upper natural slope surfaces and the conversion of the
northbound lane into a rockfall catchment area bounded by a low concrete barrier wall of
about 3 feet in height The roadway would be reconfigured for one way southbound
traffic only throughout the slope segment length The width of the catchment area would
be a minimum of about 10 feet wide adjacent to the slope The catchment area may be
sloped gently back toward the slope toe Rockfall warning signs would be posted along
the catchment area The purpose for the improvements is to develop a rockfall
catchment area below the slope to reduce the risk of falling rocks to encroach on the
roadway
The construction activity is anticipated to require road closure The existing guy pole and
drainage utilities may require reconstruction or relocation
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 27

No 2 Anchored Wire Cable Mesh
This alternative consists of the intensive scaling of loose rock and boulder materials from
the cut slope and especially the upper flatter top of slope area The intensive scaling
effort may require some demolition or site specific stabilization of overhanging rock
outcrops Additional rock bolt anchors may be needed to provide extra stabilization to
blocks of rock that cannot be removed The alternative consists of the installation of
anchored wire mesh on the cut slope face The purpose of the anchored pattern pinned
wire mesh is to provide rockfall protection through the use of a pinned wire mesh system
covering the slope face
The construction is anticipated to require traffic control including a lane closure and
protection of existing utility poles at the base of the slope Temporary barriers may be
deployed during the slope scaling to provide roadway protection
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 7

Development of a catchment area is not necessary
Disadvantages
Acquisition of some additional Right Of Way may be needed to encompass the
anchor system
Need for periodic inspection and maintenance of the anchored mesh system
Wire mesh appearance on the slope face

No 3 Shotcrete Slope Facing
This alternative consists of the intensive scaling and removal of loose rock materials
from the cut slope face and the upper natural slope surfaces Additional local slope face
treatments may include the installation of outcrop stabilizing rock bolts and the backfilling
of outcrop undercuts using Controlled Low Strength Material CLSM Following the
stabilization treatments reinforced shotcrete material would be applied as a slope facing
on the lower cut slope The upper slope surfaces would not be stabilized with shotcrete
therefore a thorough rock scaling effort is required to remove potential loose rock
hazards The purpose of the shotcrete application is to reduce the slope face exposure
to surface erosion by constructing a thin continuous layer of reinforced concrete grout
on the slope face
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with a periodic lane
closure
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 11
Advantages
Reduce erosion and provide cover of the existing exposed rock slope surface
Could be substantially constructed within the existing Right Of Way
Reduced maintenance and cleaning of soil clinker debris from the road shoulder
Catchment are not needed
Disadvantages
Need for permanent removal of vegetation from cut slope face
May require additional stabilization of potentially unstable rock blocks prior to
shotcrete application
Concrete surface appearance
Shotcrete may not be effective to resist potential large block movement over time

10
Preliminary Slope I D No
067 A
City Street Road Name
Puowaina Drive
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock cut slope is along a main roadway in a residential area The slope is composed
of fractured blocky volcanic tuff with adverse bedding sloping down toward the road
The rock slope has many potentially unstable large blocks of rock bounded by open
fractures The slope is vegetated with scattered trees including a very large banyan tree
and associated surface root network An existing concrete stairway and several lateral
utility lines traverse the slope face There is no sidewalk or curb and gutter improvement
at the site however it appears that there are some underground utilities located within
the shoulder area along the base of the slope Based on a preliminary review of property
information covering only a portion of the site the City Right Of Way is at or near the top
of slope The potential hazard consists of falling rock materials consisting of very large
blocks of rock and boulders that may slide and encroach upon the roadway and shoulder
parking area
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Soldier Pile In Fill Concrete Retaining Wall
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose rock materials from the slope and the
construction of a concrete retaining wall of about 15 feet in height along the base of the
slope In general the concrete retaining wall consists of a row of soldier piles supported
by drilled shaft foundations with concrete wall panels that are installed between the
soldier piles The concrete retaining wall should cover most of the lower and middle
slope face In place stabilization of potentially unstable blocks of rock may be necessary
for boulders rock blocks above the retaining wall height which cannot be stabilized by
scaling Prior to the wall construction the existing trees growing on the slope would need
to be removed from the site The purpose of the concrete retaining wall is to stabilize the
slope against potential rockfall hazards
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including a lane closure
Existing underground utilities and surface utility service laterals water sewer would
need to be relocated
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 18
Advantages
The alternative is considered a permanent slope stabilization and rockfall
protection measure
Improvements could be constructed within the existing Right Of Way
Minimal future maintenance and cleanup of debris

062 P
City Street Road Name
Round Top Drive
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The cut slope surfaces appear to be composed of highly to extremely weathered
cemented volcanic cinder The cut slope is along an arterial route serving a rural
residential community and scenic drive The slope is densely vegetated with shrubs and
trees and a flatter natural slope is located above the cut slope portion Based on a
preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way is mostly at the slope
toe ranging toward the middle and top of the slope Existing underground or overhead
utilities were not observed at the site The cut slope contains some large blocks about 4
to 6 feet diameter of cemented cinder that are loose and bounded by open fractures
Other portions of the slope are minimally fractured but are experiencing surficial raveling
erosion The toe of the cut slope is at the edge of the pavement with minimal shoulder
area Improvements such as curb and gutters or sidewalks are not present The potential
hazard consists of several large unstable blocks embedded within the cut slope and the
potential for eroded soils and rock fragments to encroach upon the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Slope Setback and Flattening
This alternative consists of excavating the existing cut slope to produce a minimum 10
foot wide setback from the existing toe of the slope The new cut slope is anticipated to
expose saprolitic and cemented volcanic cinder material therefore the new cut slope
may be designed with an inclination of 1H 1V or flatter The developed slope surface
could be covered with anchored erosion control matting such as Percussion Driven
Earth Anchor PDEA matting A drainage interceptor ditch should be constructed along
the top of the new cut slope to improve surface drainage The purpose of the slope
excavation is to remove the existing cut slope deficiencies such as unstable rock
material and other erosional irregularities
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including a lane closure
Existing utilities in the area are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 26

The alternative consists of the construction of a two level terraced soil nail wall retaining
system A drainage interceptor ditch would be constructed above the wall The soil nail
wall system serves as a permanent retaining wall for slopes constructed in cut condition
In general the soil nail wall consists of a series of individual reinforcing bars grouted into
drilled holes to improve the stability of an excavation or cut slope A shotcrete facing is
normally applied to the face of the reinforced excavation to provide the appearance of a
conventional concrete retaining wall The reinforcing bars provide both additional tensile
and shear strengths to the soil The reinforced soil mass behaves in a manner similar to
a gravity retaining wall but lacks a footing In general the face of the soil nail wall
retaining system is slightly battered at a slope inclination of about 1H 12V
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some road
closures The existing underground and overhead utilities may need to be relocated or
temporarily protected during construction
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 14
Advantages
Permanent slope stabilization and erosion control measure
Reduced volume of slope excavation
Create new shoulder area
Minimal future maintenance and cleanup up of erosion debris
Disadvantages
Possible need for acquisition of additional Right Of Way to encompass the
improvements
Concrete surface appearance
Permanent vegetation and tree removal from slope

No 3 Chain Link Fence at Toe of Slope
This alternative is considered to be an interim mitigation measure to reduce the potential
for rockfall debris to encroach on the public Right Of Way The chain link fence
mitigation measure could be used as an interim mitigation measure until a permanent or
long term mitigation plan for slope stabilization and or rockfall containment can be
implemented The use of standard chain link fencing should not be relied upon to
provide full rockfall protection including the catchment and retention of large falling rocks
or slippage of soil mass from the slope
This alternative consists of the installation of a standard commercial duty chain link
fence of 6 feet in height along the toe of the slope section Prior to the fence installation
manual rock slope scaling would be performed to reduce the amount of loose soil and
rocks on the slope above the fence The intent of the scaling is to provide some
stabilization of the existing slope to reduce the accumulation of soil rock debris behind
the fence in the short term Rockfall hazard warning signs would be posted along the
fence to alert the public about the potential for falling rock conditions
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some lane and
road closures
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 30
Advantages
The improvement could be constructed within the existing City Right Of Way
Relatively inexpensive improvement with low replacement cost
Effective to retain relatively small volumes of rock fragment accumulation
Preserves the natural slope face appearance
Disadvantages
Fence would not provide protection against larger falling rock high velocity rolling
rock or bouncing rocks
Fence may deform and encroach on the Right Of Way
Fence may be damaged by falling rock and require replacement
Requires periodic inspection and cleaning of entrapped debris to maintain
performance

roadway Should the potential rockfall hazard source regions on the higher slopes be

comprehensive barrier type protection system may be more appropriate The potential
hazard consists of future slope erosion that may produce high velocity rolling rock
materials that may encroach upon the roadway

shattered dike rock materials embedded within soil materials The upper half of the slope
appears to consist mostly of saprolitic and residual soils Active slope erosion and a
localized area of shallow landslide activity were observed Some existing overhead lines
utility poles drain inlets and hydrants are located along the base of portions of the
slope The existing roadway shoulders have no curb gutter or sidewalk improvements
Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way is at the

consists of falling rock materials that may encroach upon the roadway shallow depth
landslides and accumulations of weathered soil and rocky debris adjacent to the
roadway

along the lower portion of the slope Some excavation at the toe of the rock slope is
anticipated to provide space for the wall construction A drainage interceptor ditch should
also be constructed along the top of the new wall The minimum 10 foot high concrete
retaining wall should cover most of the lower and middle slope face therefore it is
critical to perform a thorough scaling of the upper slope to reduce the potential for
unstable materials The purpose of the reinforced concrete retaining wall is to
permanently stabilize the lower slope against future erosion including potential rockfall
and shallow landslide activity
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including lane closure and
contra flow of traffic Existing overhead and underground utilities in the area may need

the fence in the short term Rockfall hazard warning signs would be posted along the
fence to alert the public about the potential for falling rock conditions
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some lane and
road closures
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 30
Advantages
The improvement could be constructed within the existing City Right Of Way
Relatively inexpensive improvement with low replacement cost
Effective to retain relatively small volumes of rock fragment accumulation
Preserves the natural slope face appearance
Disadvantages
Fence would not provide protection against larger falling rock high velocity rolling
rock or bouncing rocks
Fence may deform and encroach on the Right Of Way
Fence may be damaged by falling rock and require replacement
Requires periodic inspection and cleaning of entrapped debris to maintain
performance
Difficult to perform maintenance cleaning behind the fence due to narrow
shoulder

General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The slope is on the western side of a dead end residential roadway The vegetated slope

chain link fence along the upslope side of the wall Evidence of previous boulder impact
damage was observed along the existing fence and wall Based on a preliminary review
of property information the City Right Of Way is at the toe of the retaining wall which is
privately owned The potential hazard consists of higher velocity rolling boulders from
the natural hillside that may encroach on the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Rockfall Impact Barrier on the Slope
This alternative consists of the construction of an 8 to 12 foot tall high capacity rockfall
impact barrier fence along the lower portion of the slope above the existing retaining wall
and drainage interceptor structure Consideration may also be given to placing a taller
barrier fence at the road elevation within the existing Right Of Way The configuration
would likely require sidewalk abandonment and reconfiguration of the existing roadway
to develop appropriate space for the improvements The purpose of the rockfall impact
barrier is to provide a high impact capacity flexible barrier system for the catchment and
restraint of rolling rocks and boulders from the slope
The construction may require periodic traffic control at the end of narrow lane Existing
utilities and infrastructure should not be affected by the on slope construction
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 9
Advantages
Comprehensive rockfall protection measure for the extensive slope
Only practical and viable alternative for this site condition
Option may consist of constructing the barrier at the road level by designing a
safe roadway sidewalk reconfiguration

PLATE A 21 1
A Slope ID No
21
Preliminary Slope I D No
068
City Street Road Name
Hookui Street
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock cut slope is along a sloping connector road in a residential area near
Punchbowl Crater The steep cut slope is mainly composed of bedded volcanic tuff
which is highly fractured with many loose rocks and draped with thick vegetation
overgrowth The slope height increases towards the northeast as the road drops in
elevation There is an unpaved shoulder of about 10 feet in width adjacent to the slope
Overhead and underground utilities along the slope toe were not observed The shoulder
at the toe of the slope contains accumulations of fallen cobbles and small boulder debris
Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way is at the
top middle and the toe of the slope depending on location The potential hazard
consists of falling rock materials that may encroach on the roadway or roll downhill
towards Auwaiolimu Street within the shoulder area at the base of the slope
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Anchored Wire Cable Mesh
This alternative consists of the cutting of existing thick vegetation and intensive scaling
of loose rock from the cut slope face in preparation for the placement of the anchored
wire mesh The alternative consists of the installation of anchored wire mesh on the cut
slope face The purpose of the anchored pattern pinned wire mesh is to provide slope
stabilization and rockfall protection through the use of a pinned wire mesh system
covering the slope face
The construction is anticipated to require traffic control including a lane closure
Temporary barriers may be deployed during the slope scaling to provide roadway and
public safety protection Existing utilities in the area are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 7
Advantages
Rock bolt anchors used to pin the wire mesh on the slope would aid in stabilizing
the fractured rock slope
Use of a catchment area is not necessary
Debris should be contained within the pinned mesh system
Lower debris production at the slope toe compared to the wire mesh drapery
system

materials from the cut slope face and the installation of draped wire mesh panels on the

concrete Jersey barrier wall of about 3 feet in height located about 2 to 4 feet away from
the base of the slope to develop a limited catchment area for containment of fallen
debris The purpose of the draped wire mesh is to control the fall of rock beneath the
mesh curtain toward the base of the slope and into the limited catchment area
established by the low barrier The barrier is recommended because the ground surface
at the slope toe is sloping
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including lane closure
Temporary barriers may be deployed during the slope scaling to provide roadway and
public safety protection Existing utilities in the area are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 3

Less ground anchors needed on the slope
Lower construction cost

behind the barrier

PLATE A 22 1
A Slope ID No
22
Preliminary Slope I D No
111 D
City Street Road Name
Maunawili Road
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The mixed rock and soil cut slope is composed of semi consolidated older alluvium
consisting of various weathered cobbles and some boulders embedded in a soil matrix
The slope is located along an arterial roadway that provides sole access to a residential
community Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of
Way is generally at about mid slope The existing slope has experienced significant
erosion including small landslides and the raveling of embedded saprolitic rocks from the
slope Many trees including some large leaning trees are located on the slope
Improvements such as curb and gutters or sidewalks are not present The toe of the
slope composed of loose eroded soils and some soft rock fragments appears to
encroach on the travel lane surface The potential hazard consists of eroded soils and
some falling rock debris that may encroach upon the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Anchored Wire Cable Mesh
This alternative consists of the cutting of vegetation and surface roots from the slope
face and the scaling of loose overhanging soil rock materials Anchored wire mesh
would then be installed on the existing clean slope face Due to the variable soil and
saprolitic rock composition of the slope the wire mesh drapery is anchored pinned to
the slope face to aid in the stabilization and retention of the slope materials The purpose
of the improvement is to stabilize the slope face and protect the roadway from potential
falling rock and shallow slide hazards
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with a lane closure
Existing power poles and water service utilities will need to be protected or relocated
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 7
Advantages
Minimal slope excavation
Anchored wire mesh should increase the slope stability against shallow slides
and surface erosion
Ground cover vegetation could be re established on the slope

Phase III Rock Slide Potential Inspections

Project No 01154

W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
PLATE A 22 2
Disadvantages
Acquisition of additional Right Of Way to encompass the improvements
Removal of trees from the slope

No 2 Percussion Driven Earth Anchor PDEA Matting
This alternative consists of vegetation removal and trimming of the existing topographic
irregularities from the slope face to produce a uniform slope free of the existing erosional
overhangs and landslide scars After the slope is thoroughly cleaned anchored erosion
control matting such as the Percussion Driven Earth Anchor PDEA matting would be
installed The purpose for the anchored erosion control matting is to provide an
anchored mat to preserve the slope surface and assist in stabilization of the surface soils
against shallow slips
The construction activity is anticipated to require some traffic control consisting of a lane
closure Existing power poles and water service utilities will need to be protected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 22
Advantages
Reduce surface erosion by provision of a slope cover
Assists in stabilizing the surface soil horizon against shallow slippage
Removal of existing slope irregularities that contribute to erosion and debris
production
Reduced debris clean up at slope toe
Lower construction cost
Disadvantages
Acquisition of additional Right Of Way to encompass the on slope improvements
Vegetation removal during construction with post construction vegetation
limitations
Does not stabilize against possible deeper landslide activity on the steep slopes

potential hazard consists of falling rock materials that may encroach upon the roadway
and accumulations of soil rock fragments and debris along the toe of the slopes within

barrier would be constructed along the edge of the roadway separating the new

slope and provide a shoulder catchment area for eroded slope debris

of the existing on slope overhead utility lines and poles

A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 7
Advantages
Rock bolt anchors used to pin the wire mesh on the slope would aid in stabilizing
the slope
Use of a designated catchment area is not necessary
Limited slope excavation
Consider corrosion resistant materials for coastal setting
Disadvantages

Need for periodic inspection and maintenance of the anchored mesh system
Temporary vegetation removal from the slope

No 3 Chain Link Fence at Toe of Slope
This alternative is considered to be an interim mitigation measure to reduce the potential
for rockfall debris to encroach on the public Right Of Way The chain link fence
mitigation measure could be used as an interim mitigation measure until a permanent or
long term mitigation plan for slope stabilization and or rockfall containment can be
implemented The use of standard chain link fencing should not be relied upon to
provide full rockfall protection including the catchment and retention of large falling rocks
or slippage of soil mass from the slope
This alternative consists of the installation of a standard commercial duty chain link
fence of 6 feet in height along the toe of the slope section Prior to the fence installation
manual rock slope scaling would be performed to reduce the amount of loose soil and
rocks on the slope above the fence The intent of the scaling is to provide some
stabilization of the existing slope to reduce the accumulation of soil rock debris behind
the fence in the short term Due to the very narrow existing shoulder condition some
additional excavation may be needed along the slope toe to prepare space for the fence
installation Rockfall hazard warning signs would be posted along the fence to alert the
public about the potential for falling rock conditions
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some lane and
road closures and relocation of existing utilities
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 30
Advantages
The improvement could be constructed within the existing City Right Of Way
Relatively inexpensive improvement with low replacement cost
Effective to retain relatively small volumes of rock fragment accumulation
Preserves the natural slope face appearance
Disadvantages
Fence would not provide protection against larger falling rock high velocity rolling
rock or bouncing rocks
Fence may deform and encroach on the Right Of Way
Fence may be damaged by falling rock and require replacement
Requires periodic inspection and cleaning of entrapped debris to maintain
performance
Difficult to perform cleaning of debris behind the fence due to the narrow
shoulder condition
