GEOLABS INC
PLATE A 26 2
No 2 Soil Nail Retaining Wall
The alternative involves the construction of a 3 level terraced soil nail wall retaining
system at the site The soil nail wall system serves as a permanent retaining wall for
slopes constructed in cut condition In general the soil nail wall consists of a series of
individual reinforcing bars grouted into drilled holes to improve the stability of an
excavation or cut slope A shotcrete facing is normally applied to the face of the
reinforced excavation to provide the appearance of a conventional concrete retaining
wall The reinforcing bars provide both additional tensile and shear strengths to the soil
The reinforced soil mass behaves in a manner similar to a gravity retaining wall but lacks
a footing In general the face of the soil nail wall retaining system is slightly battered at a
slope inclination of about 1H 12V A drainage interceptor ditch would be constructed
above the retaining wall
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including roadway
closures The existing overhead utility lines on the northern side of the road may need to
be de energized or temporarily relocated during the construction activity The existing
underground utilities are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 14
Advantages
Permanent slope stabilization and erosion control measure
Create some additional new shoulder area
Option for future landscaping on slope terraces
Minimal future maintenance and cleanup up of erosion debris
Disadvantages
Possible acquisition of some additional Right Of Way to encompass the new wall
Concrete surface appearance
Permanent vegetation and tree removal from slope
Higher construction cost

General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The volcanic tuff cut slope is along an arterial route serving a rural residential community
and scenic drive The slope consists of a steep cut slope adjacent to the road Other
heavily vegetated natural slopes extend upward toward the top of the ridgeline Rockfall
appears to be produced by the exposed cut slope as the hillside above generally
consists of moderately sloping lower relief terrain assumed to be mantled by cinder soils
with limited rock outcrops There are no sidewalk or curb and gutter improvements at the
site and the existing unpaved road shoulder is about 6 feet wide Based on a preliminary
review of property information the City Right Of Way is at or near the top of the cut
slope The site is opposite a scenic overlook area Existing underground and overhead
utilities were not observed at the site The potential hazard consists of potential rockfall
involving large block or slab size material from the cut slope brow that may encroach
upon the roadway

slope especially along the top of the cut slope The alternative consists of the installation
of anchored wire mesh on the cut slope face The purpose of the anchored wire mesh is
to stabilize the slope and provide rockfall protection through the use of a pattern pinned
wire mesh system covering the slope face
The construction activity is anticipated to require some traffic control including contra
flow Temporary rockfall barricades may be deployed to lessen the potential impact of
slope scaling work on passing traffic Existing utilities are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 7

the fractured rock slope

Reduced debris accumulation anticipated at the slope toe
Limited slope excavation

The rock slope is along a major urban transportation route that passes through a

along the top of the slope In addition some water meter boxes were observed at the toe

hazard consists of falling rock materials that may encroach upon the roadway and
significant accumulations of loose eroded soil and rock fragments along the road
shoulder
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Soldier Pile In Fill Concrete Retaining Wall
This alternative consists of vegetation cutting scaling of loose rock materials from the
slope removal of the slope talus and the construction of a reinforced concrete retaining
wall of about 18 feet in height along the lower portion of the slope The top of the slope
should be carefully scaled since the retaining wall would not extend the full slope height
In general the concrete retaining wall consists of a row of soldier piles supported by
drilled shaft foundations with concrete wall panels that are installed between the soldier
piles The concrete retaining wall would cover most of the cut slope face The purpose of
the concrete retaining wall is to stabilize the slope against future erosion including
potential rockfall soil erosion and shallow landslide activity
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some lane
closure or traffic contra flow fronting the site It is anticipated that the underground
utilities at the bottom of the slope and utility laterals that traverse the slope may need to
be relocated
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 18
Advantages

measure

Minimal future maintenance and clean up of debris

General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The slope is along a main roadway serving a residential community The slope consists
of a steep rock cut slope and flatter upper natural slopes extending toward the ridge
summit The cut slope contains some localized areas of loose fractured rock otherwise
the rock cut slope is in generally good condition The undeveloped and vegetated upper
natural slopes contain many large blocky rock outcrops capable of producing rolling
boulders A detailed assessment of the potential rockfall hazards on the upper slopes
may conclude that rock scaling and individual outcrop stabilization may be a viable
alternative in place of a rockfall barrier fence Existing light poles and a sidewalk are
along the slope toe Areas of GRP facing are on the cut slope face Based on a
preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way is at the cut slope toe
The potential hazard mainly consists of falling and rolling rock hazards from the upper
natural slopes above the cut slope In addition some limited potential for falling rock
hazards encompass localized areas of loose broken rock on the cut slope face
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Rockfall Impact Barrier on the Slope
This alternative consists of the construction of an 8 to 10 foot tall medium to high
capacity rockfall impact barrier fence along the lower portion of the natural slope above
the existing cut slope In addition stabilization of existing areas of loose fractured rock
on the cut slope face may be accomplished by construction of shotcrete or GRP slope
facing The purpose of the rockfall impact barrier is to provide a flexible barrier system
for the catchment and restraint of rolling rocks and boulders from the slope The purpose
of the local treatments on the cut slope face is to stabilize the identified areas of loose
rock material
The construction may require periodic traffic control Existing utilities and infrastructure
should not be affected by the on slope construction
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 9
Advantages

Limited rock stabilization work necessary on the upper slope area
Drape netting of upper slope not practical
Localized stabilization of cut slope face due to limited areas of instability

warning signs would be posted along the fenced catchment area to alert the public about
the potential for falling rock conditions

curb and gutter

retaining wall to stabilize the lower slope against shallow landslide failures and surface
soil erosion

catchment area fronting the barrier fence A 10 to 12 foot tall high capacity rockfall

because of the potential for net flexure under rock impact loading The purpose of the
rockfall impact barrier is to provide a flexible barrier system for the catchment and
restraint of potentially high velocity rolling rocks emanating from the slope
The construction should have a limited impact on traffic using a coned detour system
fronting the site except during the slope scaling work when temporary road closures
may be needed for safety reasons and cleanup of debris The proposed construction

slope located approximately 5 to 10 feet from the toe to develop a limited catchment
area for fallen boulder debris The purpose of the draped cable nets is to control the fall
of larger blocks of rock toward the base of the slope and into the limited width catchment
area established by the Jersey barrier Since the sidewalk may remain in use following
the project rockfall hazard warning signs should be posted
The construction should have a limited impact on traffic using a coned detour system
fronting the site except during the slope scaling work when temporary road closures
may be needed for safety reasons and cleanup of debris The proposed construction
should not affect the existing underground utility lines
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 6

City Street Road Name
Poola Street
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock slope is along an arterial roadway that provides access to a residential
subdivision The slope consists of a lower steep rock cut slope and an upper natural
slope containing scattered rock outcroppings A detailed reconnaissance of the upper
natural slopes should be performed to evaluate the existing slope conditions with respect
to the possible use of a rockfall impact barrier fence or use of other localized rock
outcrop stabilization methods The cut slope contains some narrow cut slope benches
and some localized areas of shotcrete treatment An existing public sidewalk traverses
the toe of the slope Based on a preliminary review of property information the City
Right Of Way is at the slope toe The potential hazard consists of falling rock materials
and rolling boulders that may encroach upon the roadway and sidewalk In addition a
near continuous accumulation of loose soil and small stones was observed on the
sidewalk along the toe of the slope segment
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Draped Wire Mesh and Rockfall Impact Barrier on the Slope
This alternative consists of vegetation cutting the scaling of loose rock materials from
the cut slope and the installation and anchoring of draped wire mesh panels on the cut
slope face In addition the alternative includes the construction of a medium to high
capacity rockfall impact barrier of about 8 to 10 feet high along the top of the cut slope
The purpose of the draped wire mesh is to control the fall of rock materials from the cut
slope toward the base of the slope at the sidewalk The draped wire mesh curtain should
extend to about the sidewalk elevation and be pinned to the slope along the curtain
bottom The purpose for pinning at the bottom of the curtain is to hold the mesh against
the slope to restrain fallen rocks within the mesh curtain and to keep larger rocks from
rolling out onto the street The purpose of the upper slope rockfall impact barrier fence is
to intercept and retain possible rolling boulders that may be generated from the upper
slope area composed of natural rock outcroppings
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control consisting of lane closure
and occasional temporary roadway closure The existing underground utilities are not
anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plates B 1 and B 9

No 3 Chain Link Fence at Toe of Slope
This alternative is considered to be an interim mitigation measure to reduce the potential
for rockfall debris to encroach on the public Right Of Way The chain link fence
mitigation measure could be used as an interim mitigation measure until a permanent or
long term mitigation plan for slope stabilization and or rockfall containment can be
implemented The use of standard chain link fencing should not be relied upon to
provide full rockfall protection including the catchment and retention of large falling rocks
or slippage of soil mass from the slope
This alternative consists of the closure of the existing sidewalk to develop a narrow
catchment area in its place The alternative also consists of the installation of a standard
commercial duty chain link fence of 6 feet in height fronting the catchment area at the
slope section Prior to the fence installation manual rock slope scaling would be
performed to reduce the amount of loose soil and rocks on the slope above the fence
The intent of the scaling is to provide some stabilization of the existing slope to reduce
the accumulation of soil rock debris behind the fence in the short term Rockfall hazard
warning signs would be posted along the fenced catchment area to alert the public about
the potential for falling rock conditions
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some lane and
road closures and relocation of existing utilities
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 30
Advantages
The improvement could be constructed within the existing City Right Of Way
Relatively inexpensive improvement with low replacement cost
Effective to retain relatively small volumes of rock fragment accumulation
Preserves the natural slope face appearance

City Street Road Name

General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The slope is on a secondary residential street The rock slope comprises a steep barren
cut and upper natural vegetated slope extending toward the top of the ridgeline The
slope is composed of weathered basalt rock ranging from massive and blocky to closely
fractured and friable Evidence of past rockfall from the cut face is apparent The
property encompassed by the slope is privately owned and currently undeveloped
Gentler talus slopes vegetated with brush front the steep cut and may aid in buffering
falling rolling rock from reaching the street An existing 6 foot chain link fence is at the
sidewalk fronting the property The fence has been damaged by previous boulder
impact Based on a preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way is
at the edge of the sidewalk The potential hazard is mainly from falling rock and rolling
boulders from the steep exposed cut slope and possibly from the upper natural slope
area which may encroach on the sidewalk and roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Rockfall Impact Barrier on the Slope
This alternative consists of the construction of an 8 to 10 foot tall medium to high
capacity rockfall impact barrier fence on the lower slope within private property
Placement of the barrier fence within the existing City Right Of Way at the sidewalk
may not leave enough clearance for possible barrier flexure towards the roadway under
impact load A minimum clearance from passing traffic of about 15 feet wide is desirable
The rockfall barrier could be constructed on the gentle talus slope encompassed by an
easement designated within the undeveloped private property The purpose of the
rockfall impact barrier is to provide a high impact capacity flexible barrier system for the
catchment and restraint of rolling rocks and boulders from the slope
The construction may require parking restrictions fronting the property Existing utilities
and infrastructure should not be affected by the on slope construction
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 9
Advantages
Provides rockfall protection from the high cut slope and lower talus slope
contained within the privately owned property

General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock slope is along an arterial roadway in a residential community The rock slope

a dense network of banyan tree root growth An existing narrow concrete drainage swale
is along the base of the slope at the edge of the pavement No road shoulder is available
and the site is on a roadway curve Based on a preliminary review of property
information the City Right Of Way varies between the top of slope and the middle of the
slope There are no public sidewalks Some existing underground utility lines are in the
roadway at the base of the slope and some existing utility sewer laterals appear to
traverse the rock slope The potential hazard consists of falling rock materials that may
encroach directly upon the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Shotcrete Slope Facing and Rockfall Impact Barrier on the Slope
This alternative consists of the removal of vegetation from the slope and the scaling of
loose rock materials from the slope face Reinforced shotcrete material would be
constructed as a slope facing If the banyan tree and root system cannot be completely
removed the shotcrete must be applied around the existing root system The purpose of
the shotcrete application is to reduce the surface erosion of the exposed slope face by
constructing a thin continuous layer of reinforced concrete grout on the slope face The
shotcrete slope facing would extend across the cut slope at the western portion of the
site
The alternative also consists of the construction of a medium to high capacity 8 to 10
foot high rockfall impact barrier across the lower talus slope at the eastern portion of the
site The rockfall impact barrier is needed within the City Right Of Way to protect against
potential rockfall emanating from a section of the cut slope located beyond the City
Right Of Way where the shotcrete cannot be constructed
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with a periodic lane
closure Utility laterals traversing the slope face may require relocation
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plates B 9 and B 11
Advantages
Could be substantially constructed within the existing Right Of Way
Eliminates erosion of the exposed slope surface and subsequent debris clean up
Lower maintenance needs expected
Lower construction cost

114 E
City Street Road Name
Old Kalanianaole Road
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The mixed rock and soil slope is along an arterial rural residential subdivision roadway
The slope is composed of mainly saprolitic soils with regions of moderately weathered
moderately to severely fractured basaltic rock Some shallow depth localized landslides
were observed involving the soils The existing roadway shoulders have no curb gutter
or sidewalk improvements Overhead utilities are on the opposite roadside Based on a
preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way is at about the middle
of the slope The potential hazard consists of some falling rock materials that may
encroach upon the roadway shallow depth landslides and accumulations of weathered
soil and rocky debris adjacent to the roadway
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Soil Nail Retaining Wall
The alternative involves the construction of a two level soil nail retaining wall system
The soil nail wall system serves as a permanent retaining wall for slopes constructed in
cut condition In general the soil nail wall consists of a series of individual reinforcing
bars grouted into drilled holes to improve the stability of an excavation or cut slope A
shotcrete facing is normally applied to the face of the reinforced excavation to provide
the appearance of a conventional concrete retaining wall The reinforcing bars provide
both additional tensile and shear strengths to the soil The reinforced soil mass behaves
in a manner similar to a gravity retaining wall but lacks a footing In general the face of
the soil nail wall retaining system is slightly battered at a slope inclination of about
1H 12V A lined drainage interceptor ditch would be constructed along the top of the soil
nail retaining wall
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control which may require lane
closure and traffic detour Existing underground and overhead utilities are not anticipated
to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 14
Advantages
Considered a permanent slope stabilization and erosion control measure
Could be constructed within existing Right Of Way
Minimal future maintenance and cleanup up of erosion debris

PLATE A 43 3
No 3 Chain Link Fence at Toe of Slope
This alternative is considered to be an interim mitigation measure to reduce the potential
for rockfall debris to encroach on the public Right Of Way The chain link fence
mitigation measure could be used as an interim mitigation measure until a permanent or
long term mitigation plan for slope stabilization and or rockfall containment can be
implemented The use of standard chain link fencing should not be relied upon to
provide full rockfall protection including the catchment and retention of large falling rocks
or slippage of soil mass from the slope
This alternative consists of the installation of a standard commercial duty chain link
fence of 6 feet in height along the toe of the slope section Prior to the fence installation
manual rock slope scaling would be performed to reduce the amount of loose soil and
rocks on the slope above the fence The intent of the scaling is to provide some
stabilization of the existing slope to reduce the accumulation of soil rock debris behind
the fence in the short term Rockfall hazard warning signs would be posted along the
fence to alert the public about the potential for falling rock conditions
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some lane and
road closures
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 30
Advantages
The improvement could be constructed within the existing City Right Of Way
Relatively inexpensive improvement with low replacement cost
Effective to retain relatively small volumes of rock fragment accumulation
Preserves the natural slope face appearance
Disadvantages
Fence would not provide protection against larger falling rock high velocity rolling
rock or bouncing rocks
Fence may deform and encroach on the Right Of Way
Fence may be damaged by falling rock and require replacement
Requires periodic inspection and cleaning of entrapped debris to maintain
performance
May be difficult to perform maintenance cleaning behind the fence due to the
very limited shoulder space

PLATE A 45 3
No 3 Slope Setback and Flattening
This alternative consists of excavating the existing steep cut slopes to produce a
minimum 10 foot wide setback at the toe of the slopes The new cut slopes may be
designed at somewhat flatter inclinations of 1H 1V or flatter to improve the slope
stability against shallow landslide activity and raveling of embedded rocks from the slope
face The new slope surfaces would be covered with anchored erosion control matting
such as the Percussion Driven Earth Anchor PDEA matting In addition the purpose of
the improvements is to correct the existing cut slope deficiencies such as cut slope over
steepening landslide scars and other erosional irregularities Finally new shoulder
areas would be created on both sides of the road to serve as a catchment area for
possible fallen debris and soil erosion
Since it may not be practical to achieve new cut slope inclinations flatter than 1H 1V
slopes of 2H 1V are considered optimal for greater slope stability because of possible
Right Of Way acquisition constraints concrete Jersey barriers are proposed to contain
potential future erosion debris away from the pavement
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with lane closure
Existing underground roadway utility lines are not anticipated to be affected Overhead
utilities may require relocation
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 26
Advantages
Improve cut slope stability by removing existing potentially unstable slope
materials and previous failure surfaces
Create new shoulder catchment area for debris thus reducing the frequency of
maintenance cleaning
Anchored erosion control matting should reduce surface erosion and shallow
depth slips
Improve roadway sight distance
Maintain natural slope appearance
Disadvantages
Acquisition of additional Right Of Way to encompass new cut slopes
Significant slope excavation required

This alternative consists of scaling of loose rock materials from the slope with greater
intensity near the top of the slope and the construction of a low concrete retaining wall
of about 3 to 4 feet in height along the toe of the slope adjacent to the existing sidewalk
The retaining wall would be backfilled close to the top of the wall and a rockfall impact
barrier fence would be constructed along the top of the new wall The rockfall impact
barrier may be a low to moderate capacity fence of about 6 feet in height The purpose
of the low wall and impact barrier system is to provide a flexible barrier against falling
rocks and a toe wall to reduce the accumulation of eroded soils on the sidewalk
The construction should have minimal impact on traffic and utility relocation is not
anticipated

Disadvantages

This alternative is considered to be an interim mitigation measure to reduce the potential
for rockfall debris to encroach on the public Right Of Way The chain link fence
mitigation measure could be used as an interim mitigation measure until a permanent or
long term mitigation plan for slope stabilization and or rockfall containment can be
implemented The use of standard chain link fencing should not be relied upon to
provide full rockfall protection including the catchment and retention of large falling rocks
or slippage of soil mass from the slope
This alternative consists of the installation of a standard commercial duty chain link
fence of 6 feet in height along the toe of the slope section Prior to the fence installation
manual rock slope scaling would be performed to reduce the amount of loose soil and
rocks on the slope above the fence The intent of the scaling is to provide some
stabilization of the existing slope to reduce the accumulation of soil rock debris behind
the fence in the short term Rockfall hazard warning signs would be posted along the
fence to alert the public about the potential for falling rock conditions
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some lane and
road closures as well existing utility protection or relocation
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 30
Advantages
The improvement could be constructed within the existing City Right Of Way
Relatively inexpensive improvement with low replacement cost
Effective to retain relatively small volumes of rock fragment accumulation
Preserves the natural slope face appearance
Disadvantages
Fence would not provide protection against larger falling rock high velocity rolling
rock or bouncing rocks
Fence may deform and encroach on the Right Of Way
Fence may be damaged by falling rock and require replacement
Requires periodic inspection and cleaning of entrapped debris to maintain
performance
May be difficult to perform maintenance cleaning behind the fence due to the
very limited shoulder space

General Description of Site Potential Hazard

cover and some trees An existing sidewalk traverses the toe of the slope Based on a
preliminary review of property information the City Right Of Way is at the toe of the
slope The potential hazard consists of falling and rolling rock materials that may
encroach upon the roadway and some accumulations of weathered soil and rocky debris
adjacent to and along the sidewalk
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Rockfall Impact Barrier at the Toe of Slope
This alternative consists of a limited scaling of loose rock materials from the slope The
existing sidewalk would be demolished and an appropriate rockfall impact barrier fence
would be constructed in its place along the slope toe The rockfall impact barrier may be
a medium capacity fence of about 8 to 10 feet in height Rockfall hazard warning signs
would be posted along the rockfall barrier alignment The purpose of the rockfall impact
barrier is to provide a flexible containment barrier for falling and rolling rocks
The construction should have a limited impact on traffic using a coned detour system
fronting the site Underground utilities at the existing sidewalk may need relocation
Existing light poles require relocation to allow for barrier net flexure under impact
loading
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 8
Advantages
Most of the improvements could be constructed within the existing Right Of Way
Easier to inspect and maintain the protection system at the roadway level
Comprehensive rockfall protection for all rock sources on the slope

Advantages
Anchors used to pin the wire mesh on the slope would aid in stabilizing the slope
against slide activity
Use of a designated catchment area is not necessary
Limited slope excavation
Natural slope appearance with provision for ground cover re vegetation

Disadvantages

Wire mesh appearance on the slope face
No 2 Soil Nail Retaining Wall
The alternative consists of the construction of a two level soil nail retaining wall with a
drainage interceptor ditch along the slope segments In general the soil nail wall
consists of a series of individual reinforcing bars grouted into drilled holes to improve the
stability of an excavation or cut slope A shotcrete facing is normally applied to the face
of the reinforced excavation to provide the appearance of a conventional concrete
retaining wall The reinforcing bars provide both additional tensile and shear strengths to
the soil The reinforced soil mass behaves in a manner similar to a gravity retaining wall
but lacks a footing In general the face of the soil nail wall retaining system is slightly
battered at a slope inclination of about 1H 12V
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including roadway
closures The existing overhead utility lines on the southern side of the road may need to
be relocated The existing underground utilities are not anticipated to be affected
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 14
Advantages
May be constructed within the existing Right Of Way
Permanent slope stabilization and erosion control measure
Reduced volume of slope excavation
Create some new shoulder space
Option for future landscaping on slope terraces
Minimal maintenance and cleanup up of erosion debris
Disadvantages
Higher construction cost
Concrete surface appearance
Permanent vegetation and tree removal from slope
SITE AND CONCEPTUAL ALTERNATIVE SUMMARY
Phase III Rock Slide Potential Inspections
Rockfall Hazard Rating System Database Update No 1
Project No 01154

W O 4683 20
GEOLABS INC
PLATE A 55 3
No 3 Chain Link Fence at Toe of Slope
This alternative is considered to be an interim mitigation measure to reduce the potential
for rockfall debris to encroach on the public Right Of Way The chain link fence
mitigation measure could be used as an interim mitigation measure until a permanent or
long term mitigation plan for slope stabilization and or rockfall containment can be
implemented The use of standard chain link fencing should not be relied upon to
provide full rockfall protection including the catchment and retention of large falling rocks
or slippage of soil mass from the slope
This alternative consists of the installation of a standard commercial duty chain link
fence of 6 feet in height along the toe of the slope section Prior to the fence installation
manual rock slope scaling would be performed to reduce the amount of loose soil and
rocks on the slope above the fence The intent of the scaling is to provide some
stabilization of the existing slope to reduce the accumulation of soil rock debris behind
the fence in the short term Rockfall hazard warning signs would be posted along the
fence to alert the public about the potential for falling rock conditions
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control including some lane and
road closures
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 30
Advantages
The improvement could be constructed within the existing City Right Of Way
Relatively inexpensive improvement with low replacement cost
Effective to retain relatively small volumes of rock fragment accumulation
Preserves the natural slope face appearance
Disadvantages
Fence would not provide protection against larger falling rock high velocity rolling
rock or bouncing rocks
Fence may deform and encroach on the Right Of Way
Fence may be damaged by falling rock and require replacement
Requires periodic inspection and cleaning of entrapped debris to maintain
performance
May be difficult to perform maintenance cleaning behind the fence due to the
very limited shoulder space

City Street Road Name
Halekoa Drive
General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock slope is along an arterial roadway serving a residential community The slope
segment consists of a weathered rock cut slope containing irregularities between the
basalt clinker and large blocks of dense rock There is an existing public sidewalk and
curb and gutter improvements at the site Some utility laterals were observed on the
slope face The toe of the slope resides adjacent to the sidewalk Based on a preliminary
review of property information the City Right Of Way is at or near the slope toe The
potential hazard consists of falling rock materials that may encroach upon the roadway
and accumulations of eroded soil and rock fragments on the sidewalk
Conceptual Design Alternatives
No 1 Soldier Pile In Fill Concrete Retaining Wall
This alternative consists of the scaling of loose rock materials including the removal of
some precariously positioned larger blocks of rock near the top of the slope from the
slope face and the construction of a concrete retaining wall ranging up to a maximum
height of about 15 feet The concrete retaining wall consists of a row of soldier piles
supported by drilled shaft foundations with concrete wall panels that are installed
between the soldier piles The purpose of the improvements is to permanently stabilize
the rock slope against erosion and rockfall
The construction activity is anticipated to require traffic control with a lane closure
Existing utility laterals that traverse the slope face will need to be protected
reconstructed or relocated
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 18
Advantages
Considered a permanent slope stabilization and erosion control measure
Minimal future maintenance and cleaning of debris from sidewalk
Disadvantages
Could be constructed within the existing Right Of Way
Higher construction cost
Utility reconstruction on the slope and below the sidewalk probable
Tall concrete wall appearance
Wall may not cover the full slope height

General Description of Site Potential Hazard
The rock cut slope is along an arterial roadway in a residential subdivision The irregular
and eroded slope is composed of layered basaltic rock with clinker seams and frequent
rock overhang conditions At the southern half of the site a series of CRM retaining
walls have been constructed to reduce debris accumulation at the sidewalk An existing
public sidewalk traverses the toe of the slope The northern half of the slope segment
has no existing retaining wall structure Several banyan trees are growing and
expanding on the slope face at the southern half of the site Based on a preliminary
review of property information the existing City Right Of Way is at or near the slope toe
Some existing underground utility laterals protected by GRP facing traverse the slope
The potential hazard consists of falling rock materials that may encroach upon the
roadway from Parcels 057 and 058 and accumulations of weathered soil and rocky
debris adjacent to and along the sidewalk from Parcel 057

No 1 Draped Wire Mesh with Low CRM Wall

the slope and the installation and anchoring of draped wire mesh panels on the slope
face The existing banyan trees and surface root networks could remain in place A low
height CRM retaining wall about 3 feet high would also be constructed at the toe of the
slope where there is no existing retaining structure The purpose of the draped wire
mesh is to control the fall of rock materials toward the retaining structures The purpose
of the low retaining wall is to provide some retention of the fallen debris and reduce the
accumulation of eroded soil materials on the sidewalk
The construction should have minimal impact on traffic and utility lateral protection is
needed
A conceptual design level drawing depicting the general components of the proposed
mitigation alternative is presented in Appendix B Plate B 2

erosion control measure

re growth of ground cover vegetation on the slope
Limited need to stabilize existing rock overhangs and slope irregularities
Existing retaining wall segment at slope toe already in place
